<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en"><i>Music</i> (Madonna album)</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

</table>
<p><i><b>Music</b></i> is the eighth studio album by American singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>, released on September 18, 2000 by <a href="/wiki/Maverick_Records" title="Maverick Records">Maverick Records</a>. Following the success of her previous album <i><a href="/wiki/Ray_of_Light" title="Ray of Light">Ray of Light</a></i> (1998), she intended to embark on a tour. However, her record company encouraged her to return to the studio and record new music before going on the road. After filming <i><a href="/wiki/The_Next_Best_Thing" title="The Next Best Thing">The Next Best Thing</a></i>, she began working on her new album, with producers like <a href="/wiki/Mirwais_Ahmadza%C3%AF" title="Mirwais Ahmadzaï">Mirwais Ahmadzaï</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Orbit" title="William Orbit">William Orbit</a>, Guy Sigsworth, Mark "Spike" Stent and Talvin Singh. <i>Music</i> has an overall <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electronica" title="Electronica">electronica</a> vibe. However, the album also contains elements of <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country</a> and <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">folk</a>, also including the use of <a href="/wiki/Vocoder" title="Vocoder">vocoder</a> on many tracks, such as "Nobody's Perfect".</p>
<p>Upon its release, the album received universal acclaim from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>, who praised Madonna's collaboration with Mirwais Ahmadzaï, as well as the album's musical creativity, however, criticizing the songs produced by William Orbit, despite calling them catchy. It was nominated for a total of five <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammys</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2001_Grammy_Awards" title="2001 Grammy Awards">2001 Grammy Awards</a>, eventually winning one. <i>Music</i> debuted at number one in over 23 countries around the world, and was Madonna's first album to reach the top of the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> in 11 years since <i><a href="/wiki/Like_a_Prayer_(album)" title="Like a Prayer (album)">Like a Prayer</a></i> (1989). It was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">three times platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA) and five times platinum by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI).</p>
<p>Three singles were released from the album; "<a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_song)" title="Music (Madonna song)">Music</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Tell_Me_(Madonna_song)" title="Don't Tell Me (Madonna song)">Don't Tell Me</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/What_It_Feels_Like_for_a_Girl" title="What It Feels Like for a Girl">What It Feels Like for a Girl</a>". All of them reached the top forty on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, with the title track peaking at number one. "<a href="/wiki/Impressive_Instant" title="Impressive Instant">Impressive Instant</a>" was released as promotional single, peaking at number one on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Play" title="Hot Dance Club Play">Hot Dance Club Play</a> chart. The album also has been included in many critic lists and polls, including <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine's "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time" title="The 500 Greatest Albums of All Time">The 500 Greatest Albums of All Time</a>", where it was ranked number 452. Alongside <i>Ray of Light</i>, <i>Music</i> was promoted by the <a href="/wiki/Drowned_World_Tour" title="Drowned World Tour">Drowned World Tour</a>, which was critically acclaimed and commercially successful, grossing around US$75 million, making it the fourth highest-grossing tour of 2001, while it received the Major Tour of the Year and Most Creative Stage Production awards nominations at the 2001 <a href="/wiki/Pollstar" title="Pollstar">Pollstar</a> awards. To date, the album has sold 15 million copies worldwide.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Music_(Madonna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guy_Ritchie_and_Madonna_(September_11_2005).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="290" data-file-width="297" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Guy_Ritchie_and_Madonna_%28September_11_2005%29.jpg/220px-Guy_Ritchie_and_Madonna_%28September_11_2005%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/28/Guy_Ritchie_and_Madonna_%28September_11_2005%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/28/Guy_Ritchie_and_Madonna_%28September_11_2005%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Guy_Ritchie_and_Madonna_(September_11_2005).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna (<i>right</i>) became involved with English director <a href="/wiki/Guy_Ritchie" title="Guy Ritchie">Guy Ritchie</a> (<i>left</i>) before recording the album.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the critical and commercial success of her album <i><a href="/wiki/Ray_of_Light" title="Ray of Light">Ray of Light</a></i> (1998), Madonna intended to embark on a new concert tour in September 1999, but due to the delay of her film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Next_Best_Thing" title="The Next Best Thing">The Next Best Thing</a></i>, that she started filming in April 1999, the tour was canceled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 1999, Madonna released a song recorded for the film <i><a href="/wiki/Austin_Powers:_The_Spy_Who_Shagged_Me" title="Austin Powers: The Spy Who Shagged Me">Austin Powers: The Spy Who Shagged Me</a></i>, called "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Stranger" title="Beautiful Stranger">Beautiful Stranger</a>". It peaked number nineteen on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> and received a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy" title="Grammy">Grammy</a> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/42nd_Grammy_Awards" title="42nd Grammy Awards">42nd Grammy Awards</a> for "<a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Song_Written_for_Visual_Media" title="Grammy Award for Best Song Written for Visual Media">Best Song Written for a Motion Picture, Television or Other Visual Media</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grammy_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-grammy-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna became involved in a relationship with <a href="/wiki/Guy_Ritchie" title="Guy Ritchie">Guy Ritchie</a>, whom she had met in late 1998 through mutual friends <a href="/wiki/Sting_(musician)" title="Sting (musician)">Sting</a> and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Trudie_Styler" title="Trudie Styler">Trudie Styler</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mirror_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-mirror-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By 2000, she was pregnant with their son Rocco. Wanting to distract herself from the media frenzy surrounding this news, Madonna concentrated on the development of her eighth studio album, entitled <i>Music</i>. Buoyed by the commercial success of <i>Ray of Light</i> album, she was keen on getting back to the studio and start recording. Madonna was well disposed towards <a href="/wiki/William_Orbit" title="William Orbit">William Orbit</a>, producer of <i>Ray of Light</i>, but by 2000, his production and sound had become ubiquitous. Also, the music scene was being dominated by younger generation of singers like <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a> and <a href="/wiki/Christina_Aguilera" title="Christina Aguilera">Christina Aguilera</a>, prompting Madonna to look for a distinctive sound in this market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obr1_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-obr1-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> It was then that she was introduced to French DJ and producer <a href="/wiki/Mirwais_Ahmadza%C3%AF" title="Mirwais Ahmadzaï">Mirwais Ahmadzaï</a>, through some common friends. Madonna instantly liked his pitch-shifting, pulverizing rhythms and his utilization of <a href="/wiki/Acid_techno" title="Acid techno">acid bass</a> in his songs. Ahmadzaï always preferred taking musical risks and hence he wanted the collaborations with Madonna to get out the best from the singer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-obr2_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-obr2-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Before the album was released, Madonna recorded a statement to her fans, stating about the album and Ahmadzaï:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>"Hey Mr. DJ, put a record on... Hi, it's Madonna. You've probably been hearing about my new record, 'Music', for a while. Well, I just wanted to make sure you knew that the single is gonna drop very soon. I worked on it with a French guy named Mirwais, and he is the shit. The album will be released worldwide on September 19, and I hope you like my music."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baby_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-baby-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Music_(Madonna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Madonna-music-sticky.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Madonna-music-sticky.jpg/220px-Madonna-music-sticky.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Madonna-music-sticky.jpg/330px-Madonna-music-sticky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Madonna-music-sticky.jpg/440px-Madonna-music-sticky.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Madonna-music-sticky.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna performing "<a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_song)" title="Music (Madonna song)">Music</a>" during the <a href="/wiki/Sticky_%26_Sweet_Tour" title="Sticky &amp; Sweet Tour">Sticky &amp; Sweet Tour</a> in 2008.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mirwais_Ahmadza%C3%AF" title="Mirwais Ahmadzaï">Mirwais Ahmadzaï</a> was introduced by Madonna's partner <a href="/wiki/Guy_Oseary" title="Guy Oseary">Guy Oseary</a>. In an interview with <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a>, she said, "Guy Oseary, my partner at Maverick [Records], was given a demo by a French artist called Mirwais," she said. "[He] slipped it to me and said, 'What do you think [of him] as an artist to sign at Maverick?' [...] I just said 'Oh my God, this is what I want.' I just flipped over it and said, 'Please find out if he wants to work with me.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna said that the producer is a "genius".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billaugust_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-billaugust-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> She also commented about working with Ahmadzaï and the other producers of the album: "I love to work with the weirdos that no one knows about—the people who have raw talent and who are making music unlike anyone else out there. <i>Music</i> is the future of sound."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bronmusic_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-bronmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Total_Request_Live" title="Total Request Live">Total Request Live</a></i>, she said Ahmadzaï was "really influenced by 1970s funk and R&amp;B" and said that the album was "more electronic than her <a href="/wiki/Ray_of_Light" title="Ray of Light">last record</a>, but it is edgier and a bit funkier."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Talking about the inspiration behind <i>Music</i>, Madonna said the album was "To join the coldness or the remoteness of living in the machine age in the world of high technology with warmth and compassion and a sense of humor. [...] <i>Music</i> is supposed to be a reflection of what's going on in society, and as far as I'm concerned, we've become too complacent."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lib_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-lib-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The album was Madonna's first album not to have been totally recorded in the United States. Instead, it was mostly recorded at Sarm West and East Studios in London, England.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-liner-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna started recording the album in September 1999, and ended in January 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bronmusic_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-bronmusic-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Mirwais Ahmadzaï spoke little English, and Madonna commented: "The first couple of days we were recording, I wanted to rip my hair out. [...] It didn't seem like there was any way for us to communicate. His manager had to come in and translate everything at first."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billaugust_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-billaugust-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Face_(magazine)" title="The Face (magazine)">The Face</a></i>, Madonna was questioned about her mood while developing the album. She commented, "To tell you the truth, I didn't know what the mood was. I feel like an animal that's, like, ready to be sprung from a cage. I've been living a pretty low-key domestic existence and I miss things. Like, I miss performing, and dancing, and being on the road, that kind of energy. So part of the record is about that. And then the other part is about love. So there's the frivolous side of my life and then there's the –hopefully– non-frivolous side of my life. I usually make a record that's one or the other, and I feel I did both on this one."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-face_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-face-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_structure_and_lyrics">Music structure and lyrics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Music_(Madonna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Music structure and lyrics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:250px; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"The first time we cut vocals, my headphones had a little reverb, but there was none on the board when they recorded me. At first, I was mildly freaked out. It sounded so raw. But then I got into the intimacy of how the vocal was presented. In fact, I got into it to the point where I insisted that there be no effects on my vocals anywhere on the album, regardless of the producer."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">Madonna about the vocoder's vocal distortion on the song "Nobody's Perfect".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billaugust_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-billaugust-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a>'s Sal Cinquemani described the album as having a "more experimental direction".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slant_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-slant-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> With <i><a href="/wiki/The_Face_(magazine)" title="The Face (magazine)">The Face</a></i> magazine, Madonna explained her inspirations behind the songs and the music of <i>Music</i>. She said, "This record, more than any other records, covers all the areas of my life. I left off partying on <i><a href="/wiki/Ray_of_Light" title="Ray of Light">Ray of Light</a></i>. But I'd just had a baby, so my mood was complete, like wonderment of life, and I was incredibly thoughtful and retrospective and intrigued by the mystical aspects of life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-face_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-face-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna also summed it up as "Funky, electronic music blended with futuristic folk. Lots of jangly guitars and moody melancholic lines."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_song)" title="Music (Madonna song)">Music</a>", the title track is the first featured on the record. Starting with Madonna's androgynous voice saying "Hey Mr. DJ, put a record on, I want to dance with my baby". Above this lyric, Madonna's voice electronically manipulated asks "Do you like to boogie woogie?" The lyric "I wanna dance with my baby" may further reinforce a connection with gay listenters. According to Santiago Fouz-Hernández in his book <i>Madonna's Drowned Worlds: New Approaches to Her Cultural Transformations</i>, "Music" is a 'disco anthem, and the beat commands [the people] to get up and dance'. He also said that the song is an expression to her public and it is one of Madonna's catchiest singles of her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-catch_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-catch-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The second track "<a href="/wiki/Impressive_Instant" title="Impressive Instant">Impressive Instant</a>" is a club-savvy stomper marked by futuristic keyboard lines and vocals that darken from distorted, and robotic passages. Madonna claimed that the song was the hardest to write.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billaugust_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-billaugust-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lib_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-lib-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna sings, "I like to singy, singy, singy, like a bird on a wingy, wingy, wingy", with childlike abandon amid a vibrant, celebratory swirl of electronic keyboard riffs and thumpy dance beats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billaugust_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-billaugust-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The third track, "Runaway Lover", is a trance/house rave track. It is one of Madonna's collaborations with William Orbit for the album. The following track, "I Deserve It", is an acoustic-framed track that is anchored by a hip-hop inflected groove. Madonna said the track "has the strangest juxtaposition of this folky, simple song and this high-tech, ominous synth line." The song lends weight to rich, introspective lyrics, such as the chorus lines: "Many miles, many roads I have traveled, fallen down of the way/Many hearts, many years have unraveled, leading up to today." "Amazing", the fifth track, is a vibrant tempo-shifter that opens with a soft, music-box-like keyboard/string flourish. The song has been compared by Madonna to "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Stranger" title="Beautiful Stranger">Beautiful Stranger</a>" (1999), saying that the reason because she fought with her record company to cancel the release as a single was because of the similarity. The sixth track, "Nobody's Perfect", includes ethereal vocals and a dreamy keyboard. The following track and second single, "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Tell_Me_(Madonna_song)" title="Don't Tell Me (Madonna song)">Don't Tell Me</a>", was written by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Henry" title="Joe Henry">Joe Henry</a>, Madonna's brother-in-law. He performed and released the track, originally named "Stop", on his 2001 album <i>Scar</i>. His wife Melanie sent a demo of the track to her sister, who liked it and recorded her version. It is framed by soft acoustic guitars and subtle keyboard lines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billaugust_8-5"><a href="#cite_note-billaugust-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The eighth track and third single, "<a href="/wiki/What_It_Feels_Like_for_a_Girl" title="What It Feels Like for a Girl">What It Feels Like for a Girl</a>", comments on female role-playing in society. The following track, "Paradise (Not for Me)", has lyrics sung in French, and the lyric "I can't remember, when I was young, I can't explain if it was wrong" reflected an artistic palette, "encompassing diverse musical, textual and visual styles in its lyrics."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fouz55_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-fouz55-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Musically, it draws influence from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edith_Piaf" title="Edith Piaf">Edith Piaf</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billaugust_8-6"><a href="#cite_note-billaugust-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was also included on Mirwais Ahmadzaï's album <i>Production</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-face_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-face-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> The tenth and final track on the album, "Gone", contrasts acoustic guitars with electronic elements. Soulful vocals give depth to such striking, cautionary lyrics as "Turn to stone, lose my faith, and I'll be gone."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billaugust_8-7"><a href="#cite_note-billaugust-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Artwork_and_release">Artwork and release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Music_(Madonna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Artwork and release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DontTellMeDionisioWeiland.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="512" data-file-width="349" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/DontTellMeDionisioWeiland.jpg/170px-DontTellMeDionisioWeiland.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/DontTellMeDionisioWeiland.jpg/255px-DontTellMeDionisioWeiland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/DontTellMeDionisioWeiland.jpg/340px-DontTellMeDionisioWeiland.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DontTellMeDionisioWeiland.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna and her dancers dressed as <a href="/wiki/Cowboy" title="Cowboy">cowboys</a> during the performance of "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Tell_Me_(Madonna_song)" title="Don't Tell Me (Madonna song)">Don't Tell Me</a>" on the <a href="/wiki/Drowned_World_Tour" title="Drowned World Tour">Drowned World Tour</a>, 2001.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For the artwork for <i>Music</i>, Madonna wore a blue shirt, jeans, red boots and a blue cowboy hat. In it, she faces the camera, while in the background a car and a gas station are seen. The <a href="/wiki/Country" title="Country">country</a> was a constant theme throughout the design, as the album's title, which was a logo that simulated a buckle, showing the silhouette of a cowboy while riding a horse and a yellow background; the bright colors give a sharp contrast compared to the photograph.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-411mania_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-411mania-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Photo sessions were conducted by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jean_Baptiste_Mondino" title="Jean Baptiste Mondino">Jean Baptiste Mondino</a>, who had worked with the singer previously on other photo shoots and music videos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Fouz-Hernández, the artwork is "a complete celebration to the field" western United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> He also added that it "is camp, notably Madonna's combination of Western clothing with expensive shoes and bright red high heels. In particular, there is a clear evocation of <a href="/wiki/Judy_Garland" title="Judy Garland">Judy Garland</a> - a major gay icon - in the artwork".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The photographs were shot in Los Angeles, between April 10 and 13, 2000. In an interview, Mondino said that he was the one who had the idea of the western themes for the album, and also stated: "[Madonna] wasn't sure at first, but I told her that if she didn't like it I won't charge her. But she loved the final result!".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The art direction and designs for the album were done by Kevin Reagan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001_Grammy_Awards_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-2001_Grammy_Awards-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2000, Madonna released a cover version of <a href="/wiki/Don_McLean" title="Don McLean">Don McLean</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/American_Pie_(song)#Madonna_version" title="American Pie (song)">American Pie</a>" (1971) as part of the soundtrack of the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Next_Best_Thing" title="The Next Best Thing">The Next Best Thing</a></i>. The song received mixed reviews, and was a success in European charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Later, the song was added as a bonus track on <i>Music</i>, except in the United States and Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-liner_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-liner-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna commented that "It was something a certain record company executive twisted my arm into doing, but it didn't belong on the [<i>Music</i>] album".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> Following the release of "American Pie", Madonna decided to use her new country style during her public appearances for <i>Music</i> '​s promotion; it included jeans, shirts and cowboy hats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> On her next tour in 2001, Madonna included a segment based entirely on this ambient.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Meanwhile, Fouz-Hernández explained that "in this appearance Madonna may be parodying and criticizing Country, which symbolizes among other things, the supremacy of the white man, the ambition of the European pioneers and the <a href="/wiki/American_Dream" title="American Dream">American Dream</a>. However, we do not realize that while recognizing the importance that the country has in American popular culture, and joins a long list of artists who have done this previously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> Despite this, the cowgirl image of Madonna has become one of its most recognized reinventions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Music</i> was released September 18, 2000, in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> on <a href="/wiki/Maverick_Records" title="Maverick Records">Maverick Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-select_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-select-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> It was released elsewhere September 19, 2000, under Maverick Records, and distributed by <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> At the same time, it was released as a limited edition which contained a 24-page booklet about the album, a brooch copper with the album's logo and two stickers, wrapped in a linen cloth available in four different colors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The Japanese edition was published on September 15, 2000, and contained two bonus tracks: "American Pie" and "Cyber-raga".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, the European version contains only "American Pie" as a bonus track.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, users who downloaded the album using Apple's <a href="/wiki/QuickTime" title="QuickTime">QuickTime</a> application had exclusive access to two remixes of "Music".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The edition published in Mexico contains as bonus tracks "Lo Que Siente La Mujer", a Spanish version of "What It Feels Like for a Girl" and a remix of the same song by the group <a href="/wiki/Above_%26_Beyond_(band)" title="Above &amp; Beyond (band)">Above &amp; Beyond</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mexico_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-mexico-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> For the Drowned World Tour, it was released as a special edition with a bonus CD with remixes and the video of "What It Feels Like for a Girl".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-touralbum_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-touralbum-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Music_(Madonna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<tr>

<tr>
<td><i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i></td>
<td style="vertical-align:middle"><span style="white-space:nowrap" title="4/4 stars"><img alt="4/4 stars" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" title="4/4 stars" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/><img alt="" data-file-height="110" data-file-width="108" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/11px-Star_full.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/17px-Star_full.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Star_full.svg/22px-Star_full.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vibe_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-vibe-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>Music</i> garnered acclaim from critics, holding a score of 80/100 on Metacritic based on 16 professional reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine" title="Stephen Thomas Erlewine">Stephen Thomas Erlewine</a> of <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> praised the album's layered music, giving it four out of five stars, and described Madonna's collaboration with Mirwais as the reason why the album "comes alive with spark and style".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic1_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic1-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Dimitri Ehrlich from <i><a href="/wiki/Vibe_(magazine)" title="Vibe (magazine)">Vibe</a></i> described the album as "a masterpiece of brilliantly arranged keyboards, futuristic drums, and electronica dressings. With folky acoustic guitars and a vaguely spiritual bent to her lyrics (like those on <i>Ray of Light</i>), it's a weird and fresh-sounding album."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vibe_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-vibe-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Andrew Lynch of Entertainment.ie, who gave the album three out of five stars, claimed that it contains "brilliant futuristic dance music", yet, claimed that the lyrics were "trite".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-entertainment1_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-entertainment1-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Robert_Christgau" title="Robert Christgau">Robert Christgau</a> gave the album an A rating, describing the tracks as "good, all chintzy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robertchristgau1_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-robertchristgau1-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Jim Farber of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> gave the album an A rating, writing that "her most patchwork record since the <a href="/wiki/Sean_Penn" title="Sean Penn">Sean Penn</a> years... In the way it tiptoes around sundry moods and beats, <i>Music</i> is frustratingly inconsistent, as if Madonna herself weren't sure where to venture next. At times, it feels like a collection of sounds -- clever, intriguing ones, to be sure -- that seek to compensate for ordinary melodies and Madonna's stoic delivery."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew1_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-ew1-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> David Browne from the same magazine claimed that it "doesn't close the book on Madonna, but it pulls only a few new tomes off the shelf."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew2_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-ew2-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> said that the album "is a much-needed breath of fresh VapoRub."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spin_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-spin-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Danny Eccleston, in a review for <i><a href="/wiki/Q_(magazine)" title="Q (magazine)">Q</a></i>, called it a "brave, radical and punchy (at a refreshing 49 minutes in length) album".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> A retrospective review in <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i> remarked: "Her first 'headphones album'… It's more playful and less pompous than <i>Ray of Light</i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> stated that the album was a rough and improvised version of <i>Ray of Light</i>, but lauded that Madonna had chosen to make a more "instinctive" record than her previous endeavours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rs_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-rs-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Mojo_(magazine)" title="Mojo (magazine)">Mojo</a></i> magazine said that "<i>Music</i> is fitful and its charms aren't all immediate, but Madonna is still doing what she does best--giving a lick of pop genius to the unlikely genre of experimental dance music."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic_41-2"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> said that <i>Music</i> is "vocodered, stretched, distorted, warped, deliberately upstaged by beats so showy they belong in a strip joint - quite simply, she's almost managed to make herself disappear. That bluntly explicit title isn't just pointless irony. This record is about the music, not Madonna; about the sounds, not the image."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nme_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-nme-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a> criticised Madonna's collaborations with William Orbit, who had worked with her on <i>Ray of Light</i>, calling them repetitive and uninteresting despite being catchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-slant_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-slant-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Music</i> earned a total of five <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> nominations. In 2001, the album won "<a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Recording_Package" title="Grammy Award for Best Recording Package">Best Recording Package</a>" and was nominated for "<a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Vocal_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Vocal Album">Best Pop Vocal Album</a>", while the title track was nominated for "<a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Record_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001_Grammy_Awards_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-2001_Grammy_Awards-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2002, Madonna received one more nomination for "Don't Tell Me" in the "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Short_Form_Music_Video" title="Grammy Award for Best Short Form Music Video">Best Short Form Music Video</a>" category. On <i>NME</i> '​s list of the 50 best albums of 2000, <i>Music</i> was ranked at number 47.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2003, the album is listed at number 452 on <i>Rolling Stone'</i>s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/500_Greatest_Albums_of_All_Time" title="500 Greatest Albums of All Time">500 Greatest Albums of All Time</a>. It is Madonna's fourth album on the list, the most among female artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Music</i> is also featured in the book <i><a href="/wiki/1001_Albums_You_Must_Hear_Before_You_Die" title="1001 Albums You Must Hear Before You Die">1001 Albums You Must Hear Before You Die</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_reception">Commercial reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Music_(Madonna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Commercial reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MadonnaParadiseFresno.jpg"><img alt="Faraway image of a blond woman singing in front of a bloomy backdrop. She is wearing a black blouse and pants of the same color. She is holding a black guitar and a microphone to her mouth." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2288" data-file-width="1712" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/MadonnaParadiseFresno.jpg/190px-MadonnaParadiseFresno.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/MadonnaParadiseFresno.jpg/285px-MadonnaParadiseFresno.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/MadonnaParadiseFresno.jpg/380px-MadonnaParadiseFresno.jpg 2x" width="190"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MadonnaParadiseFresno.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna performing "Paradise (Not for Me)" from the album on the <a href="/wiki/Confessions_Tour" title="Confessions Tour">Confessions Tour</a>, 2006.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ten days after the album's release, <a href="/wiki/CNN" title="CNN">CNN</a> reported that it had sold over four million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Music</i> debuted at number-one in 23 countries. It debuted at number one on the Billboard 200 with over 420,000 copies sold. It was the first Madonna album to reach the top of the charts in 11 years in the United States since <i><a href="/wiki/Like_a_Prayer_(album)" title="Like a Prayer (album)">Like a Prayer</a></i> (1989).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was certified <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">three times platinum</a> by the Recording Industry Association of America (RIAA) on November 21, 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaa_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-riaa-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> As of August 2010, <i>Music</i> has sold 2,925,000 copies there according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> In Canada, the album debuted at the top of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a> and was certified platinum by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Canadian Recording Industry Association">Canadian Recording Industry Association</a> (CRIA) for shipments of 300,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canada_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-canada-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout Europe, the album also did well on its charts. On October 1, 2000, <i>Music</i> debuted at number one on the Austrian Albums Chart, spending a total of forty weeks in the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-austrian_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-austrian-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> The song achieved relatively good charting in both the Flemish and Wallonian territories in Belgium, peaking at numbers two and four, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bel_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-bel-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> On the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Albums_Chart" title="French Albums Chart">French Albums Chart</a>, the album debuted at number one, staying 67 weeks on the chart, before falling out on June 29, 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-frchar_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-frchar-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> The song was certified twice platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Syndicat_National_de_l%27%C3%89dition_Phonographique" title="Syndicat National de l'Édition Phonographique">Syndicat National de l'Édition Phonographique</a> (SNEP).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fra_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-fra-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Music</i> debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK Albums Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukk_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-ukk-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was certified five times platinum by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpi_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-bpi-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> On September 28, 2000, <i>Music</i> debuted at number one on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish_Singles_Chart" title="Swedish Singles Chart">Swedish Singles Chart</a>, before falling out at number 52.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swe_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-swe-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup> Similarly in Switzerland, the album also peaked at number one, and spent 42 weeks fluctuating inside the chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swi_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-swi-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In Australia, <i>Music</i> became Madonna's fifth album to reach number one on the <a href="/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">ARIA Albums Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-austrc_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-austrc-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The album was certified three times platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Recording_Industry_Association" title="Australian Recording Industry Association">Australian Recording Industry Association</a> (ARIA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-australia_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-australia-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> In New Zealand, <i>Music</i> debuted and peaked at number two on October 8, 2000, staying on the chart for thirty-three weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nz_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-nz-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Music</i> The album debuted at number seven on the Oricon weekly album chart in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oricon_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-oricon-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Overall, in 2000, the album became the eighth bestselling album of the year,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> with worldwide sales over fifteen million copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Music_(Madonna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_song)" title="Music (Madonna song)">Music</a>" was released as the lead single from the album on August 21, 2000 by <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a>. "Music" has been praised by many contemporary critics. Some compared it with Madonna's older songs, as "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_Groove" title="Into the Groove">Into the Groove</a> (1985) and "<a href="/wiki/Holiday_(Madonna_song)" title="Holiday (Madonna song)">Holiday</a>" (1983).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sal_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-sal-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> "Music" achieved international success by topping the charts in 25 countries worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> It became Madonna's 12th number-one single on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, making Madonna the second artist to achieve number one hits in the 1980s, 1990s, and 2000s on the Hot 100. In the United Kingdom, "Music" peaked at number one on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukpeak_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-ukpeak-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> In the song's accompanying music video, comedian <a href="/wiki/Sacha_Baron_Cohen" title="Sacha Baron Cohen">Sacha Baron Cohen</a> appeared as his alter-ego <a href="/wiki/Ali_G" title="Ali G">Ali G</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The song received two Grammy nominations in the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Record_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Record of the Year">Record of the Year</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Female_Pop_Vocal_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Female Pop Vocal Performance">Best Female Pop Vocal Performance</a> categories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2001_Grammy_Awards_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-2001_Grammy_Awards-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Tell_Me_(Madonna_song)" title="Don't Tell Me (Madonna song)">Don't Tell Me</a>" was released on November 21, 2000 by Warner Bros. Records as the second single from the album. The song was written by <a href="/wiki/Joe_Henry" title="Joe Henry">Joe Henry</a>, Madonna's brother-in-law.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billaugust_8-8"><a href="#cite_note-billaugust-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> He performed and released the track, originally named "Stop", on his 2001 album <i>Scar</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billaugust_8-9"><a href="#cite_note-billaugust-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> His wife Melanie sent a demo of the track to her sister, who liked it and recorded her version. The song received positive reviews from contemporary critics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allmusic1_42-2"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic1-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> It reached at number four and spent eight weeks in the top ten of the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billbmadonna_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-billbmadonna-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The song topped the music charts in the Canada, Italy and New Zealand and attained top-ten positions on the charts of many other European nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ultratop_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-ultratop-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> The music video features Madonna walking down an automated treadmill walkway in front of a projection screen, while cowboys dance and play on the sand in the video played on the screen behind her, and was directed by <a href="/wiki/Jean-Baptiste_Mondino" title="Jean-Baptiste Mondino">Jean-Baptiste Mondino</a>. In 2005, the song was placed at number 285 on <i><a href="/wiki/Blender_(magazine)" title="Blender (magazine)">Blender</a></i> magazine's "The 500 Greatest Songs Since You Were Born".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/What_It_Feels_Like_for_a_Girl" title="What It Feels Like for a Girl">What It Feels Like for a Girl</a>" was released as the third and final single from the album, on April 17, 2001. It received positive appreciation from contemporary critics. The song lost the top-twenty on the official chart of the United States, but it was a success on the US dance charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> The music video, directed by <a href="/wiki/Guy_Ritchie" title="Guy Ritchie">Guy Ritchie</a>, portrays Madonna as an angry woman on a crime spree. Throughout the video, she is shown stealing money, driving dangerously, damaging property and setting fire to a gas station. It also has shots of pill containers and alcohol in the motel, several driving licences and Madonna putting on body armour. The final shot in the video is the car driving into a pole at full speed. Critics criticized the video for being overly violent and graphic. Madonna's spokesperson said that there was a lot of violence because it tells the story of a woman who had probably been abused. Madonna also explained that her character was acting out a "fantasy and doing things that girls are not allowed to do."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> The video was banned from most North American and European video stations including <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> and <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a>, receiving only early hours play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Impressive_Instant" title="Impressive Instant">Impressive Instant</a>" was released as a club promo only single with remixes by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Rauhofer" title="Peter Rauhofer">Peter Rauhofer</a> on September 18, 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> It went to number one on the <i>Billboard</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hot_Dance_Club_Play" title="Hot Dance Club Play">Hot Dance Club Play</a> chart where it stayed for two weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna originally wanted to release it as the fourth single, but Warner Bros. wanted "Amazing" as the next single. Madonna felt the catchiness and sound of "Amazing" was too similar to "<a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Stranger" title="Beautiful Stranger">Beautiful Stranger</a>" and wanted "Impressive Instant". Warner Bros. then planned to move forward with the release of "Amazing" without Madonna's help since she was too busy to film a music video due to prepping for her next tour. However, only a promotional CD single of "Amazing" was released in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotion">Promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Music_(Madonna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Drowned_World_Tour" title="Drowned World Tour">Drowned World Tour</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:8.DWT-Nobodys_Perfect.jpg"><img alt="Image of a brunette woman in a black-and-red kimono moving to the right of a stage with red-lit backgrounds and a metallic tree like structure in the middle. A single source of light falls on her." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="290" height="232" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/8.DWT-Nobodys_Perfect.jpg/170px-8.DWT-Nobodys_Perfect.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/8.DWT-Nobodys_Perfect.jpg/255px-8.DWT-Nobodys_Perfect.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/94/8.DWT-Nobodys_Perfect.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:8.DWT-Nobodys_Perfect.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Madonna performing "Nobody's Perfect" on the <a href="/wiki/Drowned_World_Tour" title="Drowned World Tour">Drowned World Tour</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards_2000" title="MTV Europe Music Awards 2000">MTV Europe Music Awards 2000</a>, Madonna performed "Music" while wearing a T-shirt with "<a href="/wiki/Kylie_Minogue" title="Kylie Minogue">Kylie Minogue</a>" written on it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> To promote <i>Music</i>, Madonna made two concerts titled Don't Tell Me Promo Tour. The first of these, was November 5, 2000, at <a href="/wiki/Roseland_Ballroom" title="Roseland Ballroom">Roseland Ballroom</a> in New York City, and the other November 29, 2000, at <a href="/wiki/Brixton_Academy" title="Brixton Academy">Brixton Academy</a> in London. Accompanying musicians performing with Madonna were; <a href="/wiki/Mirwais_Ahmadza%C3%AF" title="Mirwais Ahmadzaï">Mirwais Ahmadzaï</a> on guitar and longtime backing singers <a href="/wiki/Niki_Haris" title="Niki Haris">Niki Haris</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Donna_DeLory" title="Donna DeLory">Donna DeLory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyc_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-nyc-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> The costumes for the show and the set was designed by <a href="/wiki/Dolce_%26_Gabbana" title="Dolce &amp; Gabbana">Dolce &amp; Gabbana</a>. Songs performed included "Impressive Instant", "Runaway Lover", "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Tell_Me_(Madonna_song)" title="Don't Tell Me (Madonna song)">Don't Tell Me</a>", "<a href="/wiki/What_It_Feels_Like_for_a_Girl" title="What It Feels Like for a Girl">What It Feels Like for a Girl</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_song)" title="Music (Madonna song)">Music</a>". In the performance of New York, she wore a T-shirt with "<a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>" written on it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nyc_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-nyc-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna's performance at <a href="/wiki/Brixton_Academy" title="Brixton Academy">Brixton Academy</a> was shown via the internet to an estimated 9 million viewers across the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-londres_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-londres-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The song "<a href="/wiki/Holiday_(Madonna_song)" title="Holiday (Madonna song)">Holiday</a>" was added to the setlist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> The singer <a href="/wiki/Richard_Ashcroft" title="Richard Ashcroft">Richard Ashcroft</a> and the Scottish band <i>Texas</i> opened the concert.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna's performance at Brixton Academy was the last of some concert's webcasts of website MSN.co.uk that also included <a href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney" title="Paul McCartney">Paul McCartney</a>'s return to the Cavern Club - dentainer of the previous record, that was watched by 3 million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-londres_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-londres-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 21, 2001, she performed "Music" at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2001_Grammy_Awards" title="2001 Grammy Awards">2001 Grammy Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-basham_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-basham-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>To promote <i>Music</i> and <i>Ray of Light</i>, Madonna embarked on her fifth concert tour, the <a href="/wiki/Drowned_World_Tour" title="Drowned World Tour">Drowned World Tour</a>. It started in June 2001 and was Madonna's first tour in eight years since <a href="/wiki/The_Girlie_Show_World_Tour" title="The Girlie Show World Tour">The Girlie Show World Tour</a> (1993). The tour was to be started before the year 2000,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> but she had become pregnant with her son Rocco Ritchie, released <i>Music</i> that year, and married <a href="/wiki/Guy_Ritchie" title="Guy Ritchie">Guy Ritchie</a> in December 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> When Madonna finally decided to go on the tour, time was short and she had to prepare the show within three months. <a href="/wiki/Jamie_King" title="Jamie King">Jamie King</a> was signed up as the creative director and the choreographer of the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour was divided into five segments, namely <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">punk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geisha" title="Geisha">geisha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cowboy" title="Cowboy">cowboy</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_music" title="Latin music">Latin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ghetto" title="Ghetto">ghetto</a>. Each segment represented a phase of Madonna's career. Several changes were made to the final shows in Los Angeles after the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>: Madonna wore an American flag kilt during the show's opening segment as a display of <a href="/wiki/Patriotism" title="Patriotism">patriotism</a>, the closing of "Mer Girl" (part II) was altered to remove the staged shooting of a character; Madonna instead put the gun down, hugged him and they left the stage together. The macabre cannibalism-themed "Funny Song" was removed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fouz_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-fouz-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour received positive reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inder_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-inder-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour was a commercial success, grossing a total of US$75 million, and it was the top concert tour of a solo artist in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The tour received the Major Tour of the Year and Most Creative Stage Production awards nominations at the <a href="/wiki/Pollstar" title="Pollstar">2001 Pollstar awards</a>, but lost them to U2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The concert was broadcast live on <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> from <a href="/wiki/The_Palace_of_Auburn_Hills" title="The Palace of Auburn Hills">The Palace of Auburn Hills</a> in <a href="/wiki/Auburn_Hills,_Michigan" title="Auburn Hills, Michigan">Auburn Hills, Michigan</a> August 26, 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Drowned_World_Tour_2001" title="Drowned World Tour 2001">Drowned World Tour 2001</a></i> DVD was released in all regions on November 13, 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
